  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1770f85b-befe-40b5-8db7-0c3433eb44c9'

  <span id="freeText7328279963522184407" style="display:none">What if you aren’t the Chosen One?<br /><br />The one who’s supposed to fight the zombies, or the soul-eating ghosts, or whatever the heck this new thing is, with the blue lights and the death?<br /><br />What if you’re like Mikey? Who just wants to graduate and go to prom and maybe finally work up the courage to ask Henna out before someone goes and blows up the high school. Again.<br /><br />Because sometimes there are problems bigger than this week’s end of the world, and sometimes you just have to find the extraordinary in your ordinary life.<br /><br />Even if your best friend is worshipped by mountain lions...</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The book is about all the other people in the background of the story - the ones who just get on with their lives while the weird things are happening<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The book is about all the other people in the background of the story - the ones who just get on with their lives while the weird things are happening around them, think Buffy’s classmates or the rest of Hobbiton. It is also a great coming of age story!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1138398907" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138398907" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138398907?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138398907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11113379329150613379">2 1/2 stars.<br/>Here's one thing for certain: <b>Patrick Ness is a total Buffy fanboy</b>. Or possibly he hated it, but either way he paid enough attention to seemingly frame an entire book around the concept of "The Chosen One" and - specifically - Xander's quote from season 7:<br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"They'll never know how tough it is, Dawnie, to be the one who isn't chosen. To live so near to the spotlight and never step in it."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>This is a book about the people in the background. The ones who aren't "indie kids" with</span>
  <span id="freeText11113379329150613379" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars.<br />Here's one thing for certain: <b>Patrick Ness is a total Buffy fanboy</b>. Or possibly he hated it, but either way he paid enough attention to seemingly frame an entire book around the concept of "The Chosen One" and - specifically - Xander's quote from season 7:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"They'll never know how tough it is, Dawnie, to be the one who isn't chosen. To live so near to the spotlight and never step in it."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />This is a book about the people in the background. The ones who aren't "indie kids" with names like Satchel and Finn. The ones who do not get chosen, never discover their secret powers, never fall in love with a vampire, and neither save nor destroy the world.<br /><br />Each chapter opens with a short synopsis on what the "indie kids" are doing. Whether they've opened a supernatural portal, been contacted by immortals, or died. From these small paragraphs emerges a humourous parody of "The Chosen One" genre, before the chapter continues on with the everyday lives, loves, anxieties and mental health of the not chosen.<br /><br />It's a clever and interesting concept, and yet I was more in love with the idea of it than the actual execution. If I wanted to sum this book up in a single sentence, I would say: <b>Ness wrote a book about the boring, everyday kids and it was... kind of boring and everyday</b>. I wish that wasn't the case, I really do. Especially because I generally love everything Ness writes. But, if I'm being honest, by far the strongest parts of this book were the small paragraphs at the start of each chapter.<br /><br />Not that the normal kids are without sensationalism - not at all. Their lives are filled with eating disorders, OCD, car crashes, absent parents and unrequited love. But, even though the book is well-written on a technical level, I did not find their stories very compelling, or the characters themselves particularly interesting. Ness has succeeded in writing a book about people who do not stand out at all. I'm already forgetting about them.<br /><br />I feel like credit should always be given where it's due, though, and I will say that Ness has written a <b>fantastically diverse book</b>, in all senses of "diverse". I applaud him for doing so. And I also applaud him for being one of the few YA authors to write sophisticated fiction that will make teenagers think and take them to places they can't get from the mainstream bestsellers.<br /><br />I will continue to be excited when I see Ness has an upcoming release, but this one didn't quite do it for me.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11113379329150613379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1204949807" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204949807" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204949807?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=thank-you-bea-or-ala">thank-you-bea-or-ala</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204949807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5720785496992770228"><i>"I wonder what was going on last night. With the lights."<br/><br/>She shrugs. "Probably some apocalypse."</i><br/><br/>the problem with writing a book like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This' title='More Than This by Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Than This</a> is that you then have to write a book <i>after</i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This' title='More Than This by Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Than This</a>. <br/><br/>and i was a little apprehensive about this one. my copy has this cover:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1428677702l/23830990.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>which makes it look almost like a middle grade book, and i was concerned that it wouldn't live up to the mind-shattering acrobatic metafiction that was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This' title='More Than This by Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Than This</a>.<br/><br/>and it doesn't. nothing ever will.<br/>but that doesn't mea</span>
  <span id="freeText5720785496992770228" style="display:none"><i>"I wonder what was going on last night. With the lights."<br><br>She shrugs. "Probably some apocalypse."</i><br><br>the problem with writing a book like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This" title="More Than This by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than This</a> is that you then have to write a book <i>after</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This" title="More Than This by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than This</a>. <br><br>and i was a little apprehensive about this one. my copy has this cover:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1428677702l/23830990.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>which makes it look almost like a middle grade book, and i was concerned that it wouldn't live up to the mind-shattering acrobatic metafiction that was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This" title="More Than This by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than This</a>.<br><br>and it doesn't. nothing ever will.<br>but that doesn't mean this isn't a great book all on its own. <br><br>this book plays with the literary convention of the "chosen one," - those who are set apart from their peers and tasked with a responsibility no less than that of saving the world. and they wrestle with this burden and forgo having a normal adolescent life because they are the only ones who can do what needs to be done and they fight evil and deputize their friends in the struggle and still manage to pass their math tests.<br><br>this book is not about the chosen ones.<br>this book is about the blurry kids in the background of the wide-angle shots - the ones who are just hurrying to class.<br><br>it's about these people:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/buffy_graduation_day_zpsbz5vict1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434215657i/15184262._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo buffy_graduation_day_zpsbz5vict1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>they attend the same school as the chosen ones, and they witness the horrors that seem to follow "the indie kids*" around, but they are uninvolved in their exploits, in their occasional demises. on the sidelines, all they can do is remark is that <i>"They better not blow up the high school again."</i><br><br>the trials of the indie kids open each chapter, with a brief synopsis of what is going on in their struggle while the book itself is primarily concerned with bringing the blurry kids into the spotlight to show that, yeah, there's a portal of doom opening in the gymnasium, but other things are happening in what would ordinarily be the background, and those struggles are every bit as challenging as the ones centered around the portal. people have eating disorders, OCD, distant or absent parents, unrequited love, car accidents. and these things <i>matter</i>.<br><br><i>"Not everyone <b>has</b> to be the Chosen One. Not everyone has to be the guy who saves the world. Most people just have to live their lives the best they can, doing the things that are great for <b>them</b>, having great friends, trying to make their lives better, loving people properly. All the while knowing that the world makes no sense but trying to find a way to be happy anyway."</i><br><br>it's a great blend of fantasy and contemporary fiction, as the separate storylines overlap and commingle: jealousy and zombie deer, the alzheimer's of a beloved grandmother and strange blue glows, bickering and bombs, prom and portals. there's a little cheating, since one of the "normal" kids is also a descendant of the goddess of cats and has a couple of powers of his own, but for the most part, the problems are familiar ones, and they are dealt with in mortal ways.<br><br>being a long-time lover of cheesy teen horror movies, and having finally caved last year and watched buffy, there were plenty of nods, references, and allusions to the chosen one genre that i really appreciated, but i appreciated even more ness' little reversals.<br><br><i>"Now you're <b>sure</b> we're not going to be ritualistically murdered?…Prom night. Group of diverse teens. Remote cabin…"<br><br>…"That's not the story that's happening," Mel says to him. "We're not the kind of people that story happens to."</i><br><br>it's a fun, clever book, and while it's no <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This" title="More Than This by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than This</a>, it's way more than it appears.<br><br><br><br>* an rare unfortunate decision on ness' part, IMHO.<br><br>*******************************************************<br><br>well, he hasn't failed me yet.<br><br>and <i> the God of mountain lions</i>???<br><br>even if that's just a figure of speech, i'm sold.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5720785496992770228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4906675052025534563">This is my first Ness book, and maybe I picked the wrong book.<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong. This book wasn't <i>bad</i> bad, not in a way that would make me rant and rage about how awful it is. It just wasn't to my taste. His writing style doesn't connect with me. The book was weird, and, dare I say it before a legion of Ness fans with pitchforks descend upon me, really boring.<br/><br/>I just don't get it. Again, not my style. I prefer excitement, a definable plot, well-written emotions and interactions, and this book wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4906675052025534563" style="display:none">This is my first Ness book, and maybe I picked the wrong book.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong. This book wasn't <i>bad</i> bad, not in a way that would make me rant and rage about how awful it is. It just wasn't to my taste. His writing style doesn't connect with me. The book was weird, and, dare I say it before a legion of Ness fans with pitchforks descend upon me, really boring.<br /><br />I just don't get it. Again, not my style. I prefer excitement, a definable plot, well-written emotions and interactions, and this book was a lot of strangeness and too much dialogue and characters I couldn't connect to.<br /><br />I like my books with a purpose, and I suppose the esteemed Patrick Ness' style is just not for me. </span>

<div id="review_1241315199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1241315199" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1241315199?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1241315199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8223952223925785140">Oh wow, oh wow, oh wow. <b>This book is incredible and emotional and relatable and OH WOW.</b> How does Patrick Ness write like this?! (Answer: he is a wizard.) I've loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8621462.A_Monster_Calls' title='A Monster Calls by Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Monster Calls</a> and<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8621462.A_Monster_Calls' title='A Monster Calls by Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Monster Calls</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This' title='More Than This by Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Than This</a>. So I was like 99% sure that I'd adore <i>The Rest Of Us Just Live Here.</i> But I didn't actually know what it was ABOUT, except it was NOT about "The Chosen One". And I had noooo idea it was about families and sibling relationship and end-of-school and anxiety. So, give me a moment. I </span>
  <span id="freeText8223952223925785140" style="display:none">Oh wow, oh wow, oh wow. <b>This book is incredible and emotional and relatable and OH WOW.</b> How does Patrick Ness write like this?! (Answer: he is a wizard.) I've loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8621462.A_Monster_Calls" title="A Monster Calls by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">A Monster Calls</a> and<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8621462.A_Monster_Calls" title="A Monster Calls by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">A Monster Calls</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786.More_Than_This" title="More Than This by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than This</a>. So I was like 99% sure that I'd adore <i>The Rest Of Us Just Live Here.</i> But I didn't actually know what it was ABOUT, except it was NOT about "The Chosen One". And I had noooo idea it was about families and sibling relationship and end-of-school and anxiety. So, give me a moment. I just need to hug this book and pronounce it a new favourite.<br /><br /><blockquote> "Not everyone <i>has</i> to be the Chosen One. Not everyone has to be the guy who saves the world. Most people just have to live their lives the best they can, doing things that are great for <i>them</i>, having great friends, trying to make their lives better, loving people properly. All the while knowing that the world makes no sense but trying to find a way to be happy anyway."</blockquote><br /><br /><b>It's set in the kind of world that's HAD all the weird superhero stuff happen.</b> But it happened in the last generation or no one really believed it or it got covered up as some sort of accident. So everyone <i>believes</i> in supernatural stuff, but they don't. (Am I confusing? TELL ME THIS MAKES SENSE.) Which I think is an epic story world. Although, there was lots of weight on the fact that there's "indie kids" and "normal kids". I <i>guess</i> (and asked around) that "indie kid" just means the hipster kid. So the Peter Parker kind of dude? <i>Anyway</i>. That threw me because I'd never heard the term "indie kid" and it was weird. BUT ANYWAY. <br /><br />This story focuses on a foursome of completely-incredibly normal kids. Except, of course, for the tiny fact that they're not. <br /><br />So can we talk about the characters?! YES AND PLEASE AND THANK YOU. <br /><br /><b> + Mikey:</b> He's the narrator. He's, like, incredible. He's the quiet one, the one who feels replaceable. He has serious OCD and unrequited love with his sister's best friend and, he's just adorable. The way he loves his sisters and takes care of them?! I ADORE HIM. <br /><b> + Mel:</b> Yes, the entire family has names that start with M. Worse, their last name is Mitchell. Nuuuuungh. (Although I think that's done on purpose.) SO. Mel has had anorexia...basically anxiety. The family is built on anxiety, it's really sad and entirely relatable. I really connected to both Mel and Mikey. Their relationship is SO CLOSE, and they're there for each other when the other is having an anxiety episode. I love sibling relationships. Have I ever mentioned that?! I LOVE 'EM. I also really loved that the book wasn't <i>about</i> Mel falling into anorexia again. It was about her journey of moving forward. A lot of the time I feel like books are continually about the decline into the abyss. So it's nice when they're about the hard crawl upwards.<br /><b> + Meredith:</b> She's the 10 year old, youngest. And she's adorable. She's passionate and clever (like, she's a genius) and I LOVED how the teens included her. It wasn't a "oh my gosh, I haaaate it when my little sister is hanging around". They all loved her and took care of her. It was so so sweet. FJDAJKLS TO THIS ADORABLE FAMILY. <br /><b> + The Mitchell Parents:</b> yeah, except they were dead losses. Which is odd considering how wonderful their children are. Hmm. The father is an alcoholic who's basically mentally checked out of the family. The mum is so deep into politics nothing else matters for her. <br /><b> + Jared:</b> I liked Jared. He was a really epic best friend for Mikey. He's gay and big and kind and totally there for Mikey with his anxiety. They make it clear they're <i>not a couple</i> although you can definitely see they love each other. I guess they love each other in a family way. Buuuut...I had my doubts sometimes. I also got SO MAD at Jared several times. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Like when he loses it at Mikey and says how needy and clingy and whiny Mikey is. When he's <i>not</i>. And you have to know, for someone with anxiety, being told their worst fears are true is like driving a spork through their heart. He HURT Mikey as hard as he could....I know Mikey was being a pain at that point, with Jared/Nathan. But seriously?! I lost respect for Jared there. And I also can't figure out whey they didn't tell Mikey it was Jared/Nathan instead of Nathan/Henna. LIKE, WHAT??? WHY? So stupid. Teenagers. UGNNNNHG. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b> + Henna:</b> Okay, out of the foursome (Mel, Mikey, Jared and Henna) I really didn't like her the most. I felt like she lead Mikey on at the same time as friendzoning him. I think their relationship was interesting...not quite romantic. Very unrequited. But yet...so unique and different. IT'S COMPLICATED. But it actually was! Their feelings were. And, duuuude, that's refreshing to read, okay? Henna was black and vibrant and had parents who were missionaries and she was half Scandinavian. <br /><br />There is a lot of diversity. Which is great. And it was natural and interesting and flowed.<br /><br /><b>Despite the "superhero" background...that's all it is. A BACKGROUND.</b> It seriously doesn't dive into that side of things. Each chapter starts with this paragraph about what the superheroes are doing...nearly a cliche stereotypical monologue. Which I found insanely interesting. And then it'd get back to the complex and difficult and filled with anxious worried lives of the foursome. I LOVED IT. <b>I loved how the author handled anxiety.</b> I loved how the story was focused on family and moving on and growing up and <i>love</i> -- but the complicated kind of love. It's not a massively fast story, but it's addicting.<br /><br />OH IT'S SO ADDICTING. <br /><br />I felt so emotionally invested. I connected to, like, all the characters (but the Mitchell family particularly stole my heart) and I just felt the book was suffocatingly perfect. Like, if you've ever experienced anxiety -- THIS book gets it right. And plus the writing is just gorgeous. It's heavy on the dialogue and doesn't waste time and knows how to hook you in with just a few words. It's a little big magical and yet 100% real. (Trust me, that's totally plausible.) There's weirdness and normality. <br /><br /><b>WHAT ARE WORDS?! JUST GO READ IT.</b> This is one you <i>need</i> in your life. Just have chocolate on hand. I need chocolate. SOMEONE GET ME CHOCOLATE. <br /><br />*breaks down sobbing over perfectness of book*</span>
  <a data-text-id="8223952223925785140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2204124482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2204124482" />
    <a title="Helen 2.0" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0"><img alt="Helen 2.0" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553725p2/39575951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2204124482?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=kayla">kayla</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2204124482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9819559108827431257">This book claims to be a parody of popular YA books that feature OTT heroines and plotlines. The main characters go to high school in a world much like our own, except for the indie kids. Indie kids are the nerds with glasses, the disgraced prom queens, the child prodigies - all those teens that always end up as protagonists in a bad YA novel. Every few years, the indie kids will thwart some alien/vampire/ghost invasion and save the world, killing some unimportant side characters and usually blo</span>
  <span id="freeText9819559108827431257" style="display:none">This book claims to be a parody of popular YA books that feature OTT heroines and plotlines. The main characters go to high school in a world much like our own, except for the indie kids. Indie kids are the nerds with glasses, the disgraced prom queens, the child prodigies - all those teens that always end up as protagonists in a bad YA novel. Every few years, the indie kids will thwart some alien/vampire/ghost invasion and save the world, killing some unimportant side characters and usually blowing up the school while they're at it. The school is rebuilt, funerals are held, and a few months later everyone has forgotten anything unusual ever happened.<br /><br />The Rest of Us Just Live Here focuses on the regular students. Mickey is a high school senior who just wants to graduate before the indie kids get anyone else killed. The story revolves mostly around Mickey's crush on a female friend, as well as the problems of his family and close friends. <br /><br />The premise is really creative. A YA book that's about the Muggles, the normies, the stunt doubles? Brilliant. Each chapter begins with a heading describing what the resident indie kids are up to, saving the world from aliens and accidentally unleashing terrible attacks on the regular population. <blockquote>
  <i></i>
</blockquote><br />These headings were probably my favorite part of the book. It was so much fun to hear about these massive plot points being referenced marginally by people as ordinary as Mikey and co. It was like following a citizen on presidential election day and hearing them say "Is something going on today? What are all these people doing out on the street?"<br /><br />In many ways this book was reminiscent of Rainbow Rowell's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32768522.Carry_On__Simon_Snow___1_" title="Carry On (Simon Snow, #1) by Rainbow Rowell" rel="nofollow noopener">Carry On</a>. The tone, the premise, especially the focus on deep <s>angsty</s> emotion and mental health. I wasn't happy with the resemblance, since I've never been a fan of the was Rainbow Rowell writes teen narrators. Who in their life ever met a teen as self-aware, as eloquent, or as deeply emotional as RR's main characters? All of Patrick Ness's characters are equally unrealistic, which was off-putting. <br /><br />All in all, I liked it, but not as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20758104.The_Knife_of_Never_Letting_Go__Chaos_Walking___1_" title="The Knife of Never Letting Go (Chaos Walking, #1) by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">The Knife of Never Letting Go</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9819559108827431257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1468022905" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1468022905" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1468022905?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=with-a-touch-of-paranormal">with-a-touch-of-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1468022905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3373097372483717835"><br/><b> <i> “Not everyone has to be the guy who saves the world. Most people just have to live their lives the best they can.” </i></b><br/><br/>If there’s a word that would best describe author, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/370361.Patrick_Ness' title='Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patrick Ness</a>, it would be <u>
  <b>ingenious.</b>
</u> True, the story may not have the most adventurous plot but the premise sure is brilliant and completely original. I have personally never thought about the side characters, the ordinary people watching Katniss and Peeta fight for their lives in the hellish arena…<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450053348i/17372108._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>...or the kid watching Spide</span>
  <span id="freeText3373097372483717835" style="display:none"><br><b> <i> “Not everyone has to be the guy who saves the world. Most people just have to live their lives the best they can.” </i></b><br><br>If there’s a word that would best describe author, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/370361.Patrick_Ness" title="Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Ness</a>, it would be <u>
  <b>ingenious.</b>
</u> True, the story may not have the most adventurous plot but the premise sure is brilliant and completely original. I have personally never thought about the side characters, the ordinary people watching Katniss and Peeta fight for their lives in the hellish arena…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450053348i/17372108._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...or the kid watching Spiderman fight the bully at the school hall.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450053508i/17372136._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> I doubt anyone has ever thought about them, like really thought of them until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/370361.Patrick_Ness" title="Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Ness</a>.<br><br>This creative story is inventively about a group of teenage non-heroes, the none “Indie” kids who try to just live their ordinary lives in a small town where zombies, soul eating ghosts and vampires are daily ordinary occurrences and where the Indie kids die off one after the other but which isn’t a huge deal because the non-heroes are not really affected, unless they become one of the “casualties.”<br><br>At first, I found the story kind of weird and confusing because of the unique structure with a small side story about the Indie kids at the start of each chapter, but not long after (when I finally got the hang of it), I started to really enjoy it because the writing is surprisingly easy and funny to read. The lack of action in the plot makes perfect sense because the focus of the story is the personal struggle of the individual characters who may not have been chosen as heroes but who are still heroes of their own lives. <br><br>I was surprised at the amount of social issues that were effectively tackled in the novel despite the light and comic tone. I was also impressed at the fullness of the development of the characters despite the relatively few pages (for a sort of apocalyptic novel) and satisfied at the conclusion that would make this standalone contemporary/slight apocalyptic novel one of a kind. <br><br>Lastly, I learned from the Author’s Note that the author auctioned off the chance to have the winner’s name in the book for a Red Cross fund raising project to help the countless victims of typhoon Haiyan that devastated the Philippines in 2013. :,) I think I officially love Patrick Ness now. &lt;3<br><br>Thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1313910299?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Will’s excellent review</a> that made me read the book. Do check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025313633?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil’s awesome review</a> too.<br> <br> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3373097372483717835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420269045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12792884160828432013">So, since this got a bunch of good reviews, I decided to pick this up. Just my luck that Target would have autographed first editions of it:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445271745i/16623515._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445271745i/16623516._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The basic premise of this book is that the main characters here are the background players in everything else. The funny thing is that this story, while YA, makes fun of YA tropes and bloated subgenres like vampires or demigods or immortals and kids "dying beautifully of cancer". That's the whole joke about this book is that it's poking fun at how airheaded </span>
  <span id="freeText12792884160828432013" style="display:none">So, since this got a bunch of good reviews, I decided to pick this up. Just my luck that Target would have autographed first editions of it:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445271745i/16623515._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445271745i/16623516._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The basic premise of this book is that the main characters here are the background players in everything else. The funny thing is that this story, while YA, makes fun of YA tropes and bloated subgenres like vampires or demigods or immortals and kids "dying beautifully of cancer". That's the whole joke about this book is that it's poking fun at how airheaded YA culture can be sometimes, how teens can mindlessly go after the next big thing and turn it into a plague that destroys their brain cells while parents pretend it isn't happening.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445874165ra/16713007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's as if the camera were to pan away from Bella and Edward and start following Anna Kendrick and all of the other nobody characters (but without all of the tryhardness of IRL Anna Kendrick that gets really obnoxious). <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22910900.The_Rest_of_Us_Just_Live_Here" title="The Rest of Us Just Live Here by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rest of Us Just Live Here</a> is about the people who have to watch from the sidelines and are never part of the larger story, which is probably why this book is very popular: it speaks to all the people who weren't popular in school.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12792884160828432013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1025313633" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025313633" />
    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025313633?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062415639" href="/book/show/24723317-the-rest-of-us-just-live-here">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=i-loved-it-aka-all-time-faves">i-loved-it-aka-all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=books-from-my-favorite-authors">books-from-my-favorite-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025313633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8720390614651024542">The Rest of Us Just Live Here is a weird-and-not kind of book. I mean it's weird because it's not about the Chosen Ones (or the indie kids as this novel called them) and it's not weird because it's not about the Chosen Ones. (You got me?)<br/><br/>In this world we live in, we would rather read a kick-ass hero/heroine who saves the world than reading a bunch of <s>boring</s> kids who want to graduate high school, no? This is the main concept of this book. So, if you're not into this kind of novel, you will probab</span>
  <span id="freeText8720390614651024542" style="display:none">The Rest of Us Just Live Here is a weird-and-not kind of book. I mean it's weird because it's not about the Chosen Ones (or the indie kids as this novel called them) and it's not weird because it's not about the Chosen Ones. (You got me?)<br /><br />In this world we live in, we would rather read a kick-ass hero/heroine who saves the world than reading a bunch of <s>boring</s> kids who want to graduate high school, no? This is the main concept of this book. So, if you're not into this kind of novel, you will probably not enjoy this one. (But who knows, right?) Me? I really did enjoy and appreciate this novel. Because, I kinda relate to the main characters' feelings. And I can share the same sentiments with them.<br /><br />But seriously, this book is weiiiiiiiird because the main characters (not the indie kids) were living their ordinary lives in a world where there's something strange and extraordinary is happening. Something that include Immortals, Gods, zombie deers, etc. If you think about it, this is cool even you are just the ordinary kids who wants to graduate and not the Chosen Ones who will save the town or the world.<br /><br />As a reader who can't really describe things well, I found myself captivated and fascinated by this book. The original plot, the beautiful writing, the diverse characters, the intriguing setting, the funny dialogues, the mystery, the lessons and insights. All of it. I love them all. But, I do really love how Ness tell this story. The emotion inserted in every word that made my reading experience so so damn good. The Rest of Us Just Live Here seemed ordinary but actually, it is extraordinary.<br /><br />As a conclusion, I think the book's main goal is to impart the insight of living your life to the fullest, in a cliche-or-not way. Which you shouldn't forget that even you aren't a hero that will save the world, you are the hero of your life. You are extraordinary and most importantly, you are loved. By many.</span>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406361797" href="/book/show/26117652-the-rest-of-us-just-live-here">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313910299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12284260061039948886">Contemporary YA is not my genre, but this novel was an exception. I prejudged it based on the first few chapters, but as the plot developed, I started to like it. <br/><br/>This is a novel about a group of friends who wants to have a normal life. They just want to graduate before the school blows up. Mysterious and paranormal things get in their way, but they did all they could to succeed.<br/><br/>What was most striking to me was the fact that Ness managed to incorporate a lot of serious issues in this novel. It w</span>
  <span id="freeText12284260061039948886" style="display:none">Contemporary YA is not my genre, but this novel was an exception. I prejudged it based on the first few chapters, but as the plot developed, I started to like it. <br /><br />This is a novel about a group of friends who wants to have a normal life. They just want to graduate before the school blows up. Mysterious and paranormal things get in their way, but they did all they could to succeed.<br /><br />What was most striking to me was the fact that Ness managed to incorporate a lot of serious issues in this novel. It was supposed to be a fun novel, but it was both fun and eye opening. He tackled multiple issues like depression, anxiety, and more. The novel was a mixture of laughter and sadness. Near the end was the part of sadness creeping in.<br /><br />I really liked how the characters developed and how they were connected to each other. I always ask for a novel with good characters, and this one has that. the transformation of the main character was commendable. He became a lot independent and wise, as compared to what he was in the first few chapters.<br /><br />The plot was light and straightforward. The premise didn't wander off from its promise, so it's not disappointing in that aspect. The plot was too simple though, for me. Ness could've added more interesting elements, and that would've made me give this a higher rating.<br /><br />4/5 stars. Impressive new novel from Patrick Ness. I enjoyed most of his other novels, so it wasn't a surprise that I enjoyed this one too. It's always a whole lot of guessing when it comes to Ness. Like how I kept on guessing how the novel was going to end. Things didn't go my way, but I liked how he ended things.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12284260061039948886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1257925661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257925661" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257925661?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25207164-the-rest-of-us-just-live-here">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-complete">r2r-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257925661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6875635395675323235">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“On the day we’re the last people to see indie kid Finn alive, we’re all sprawled together in the Field, talking about love and stomachs.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380999712i/3753648.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This may be one of the most pointless books I have ever read.<br/><br/>Poor Mike had problems, he had OCD, his sister had nearly died due to anorexia, and he was in love with his best friend but didn’t have the guts to tell her. The rest of the </span>
  <span id="freeText6875635395675323235" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“On the day we’re the last people to see indie kid Finn alive, we’re all sprawled together in the Field, talking about love and stomachs.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380999712i/3753648.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This may be one of the most pointless books I have ever read.<br><br>Poor Mike had problems, he had OCD, his sister had nearly died due to anorexia, and he was in love with his best friend but didn’t have the guts to tell her. The rest of the story though, was not only confusing, it was also pretty dull.<br><br><b>
  <i>“I wash again in the exact same order. Third time through, I know I’m gone. Forehead, nose, cheekbones, chin, neck. Forehead, nose, cheekbones, chin, neck. Forehead, nose, cheekbones, chin, neck. Shit shit shit shit shit.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436116980i/15420927.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this was about Mike’s life, but other than one incident, there wasn’t a lot happening. The story seemed to drop us right in the middle of something at the beginning, to the point where I turned back pages to make sure I hadn’t missed something, and then there was words thrown in there with no explanation of what the heck they meant! I mean this was like maze-runner all over again! What the heck is an ‘Indie’ kid? And why do they dislike them so much? Is it a race? Is it a word for kids from the wrong side of the tracks? Or what? Because I’ve read the whole book and still can’t work it out!<br><br><b>
  <i>“There are two more dead indie kids. I didn’t really know either of them.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436116980i/15420928.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there was the weird paranormal stuff that suddenly came into things. What the heck were the animals and people with weird glowing eyes about? What connection did they have to the murders of the indie kids? I’m guessing that this is supposed to be a story about the lives of normal people, while something paranormal is going on that they’re not involved in? Possibly? But the problem is, that if the normal people’s lives are so interesting that they require a book, why do we even need anything else going on? And why can’t you freaking tell us what’s going on instead of dropping in random weird occurrences, and never telling us what they mean? Can you tell that this has annoyed me?<br><br><b>
  <i>“It’s eyes glow blue, actually glow, and on my back in a soggy ditch as it stands over me, it’s pretty much all I can do not to wet myself.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410527822ra/11119544.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this was also confusing, and I just felt that if anything interesting had happened in this book, we weren’t told about it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434917067i/15278160.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>4.5 out of 10</span>
  <a data-text-id="6875635395675323235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1628489034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1628489034" />
    <a title="may ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49148508-may"><img alt="may ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562443036p2/49148508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1628489034?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=300-pgs">300-pgs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=real-problems">real-problems</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1628489034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17766586351091897745"><br/>My very first buddy read with my favourite, the lovely <i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/48546428-annie-a-court-of-mist-books' rel='nofollow noopener'> Lady Pim (aka Annie) of the Book Court</a> </i><br/><br/><br/>Looking for a book that’s ridiculously relatable?? I found it. <br/><br/><i> “What do you do when your dreams are about to come true?” she asks. “No one ever tells you. They tell you to chase them, but what happens when you actually catch one?” </i><br/><br/>So many of the books we read center around the <b> Chosen-One™, the Special-Snowflake™, the Saviour-of-the-World™, </b> but this book is just about the everyday kids (basically an</span>
  <span id="freeText17766586351091897745" style="display:none"><br>My very first buddy read with my favourite, the lovely <i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/48546428-annie-a-court-of-mist-books" rel="nofollow noopener"> Lady Pim (aka Annie) of the Book Court</a> </i><br><br><br>Looking for a book that’s ridiculously relatable?? I found it. <br><br><i> “What do you do when your dreams are about to come true?” she asks. “No one ever tells you. They tell you to chase them, but what happens when you actually catch one?” </i><br><br>So many of the books we read center around the <b> Chosen-One™, the Special-Snowflake™, the Saviour-of-the-World™, </b> but this book is just about the everyday kids (basically and me you) who usually get overlooked. <br><br><i> The Rest of us Just Live Here </i> is narrated by Mikey, a regular senior who is about to graduate with his sister and his best friends, Jared and Henna. With their impending (very frightening but very normal) future becoming a reality, the group is trying to live out their final week together.<br><br>But while Mikey stresses over asking out his long-time-crush Henna out, an End-of-the-World sort of event is taking place (hence the crazy blue lights). <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482245344i/21497108._SY540_.png" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really enjoyed reading this book for the reason that it was very relatable. While Mikey doesn’t have the burden of saving the world, he is fighting other battles like his un-perfect family and his OCD. <br><br>But Patrick Ness doesn’t leave us clueless as to what the real heroes have to encounter. With each chapter, we get a brief summary of what the <i> Indie Kids </i> are doing and what’s happening in the world of the <i> Chosen Ones. </i> And I must say, I mightily enjoyed that. <br><br>I particularly liked how the plot was centered around the theme of friendship and love and family. Cheesy as it sounds, it was very heartfelt and inspiring. <br><br>A very pleasant and easy read (with a lovely touch of hilarity). <br><br><i>“Not everyone has to be the Chosen One. Not everyone has to be the guy who saves the world. Most people just have to live their lives the best they can…” </i><br><br><br><br>3.5 stars!!!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17766586351091897745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2228253940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2228253940" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2228253940?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25207164-the-rest-of-us-just-live-here">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2228253940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14274896039657999782"><i> “The Indie Kids, huh? You’ve got them at your school, too. That group with the cool-geek haircuts and the thrift shop clothes and names from fifties. Nice enough, never mean, but always the ones who end up being the Chosen One when the vampires come calling or when the alien queen needs the Source of All Light or something. They’re too cool to ever, ever do anything like go to prom or listen to music other than jazz while reading poetry. They’ve always got some story going on that they’re heroe</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14274896039657999782" style="display:none"><i> “The Indie Kids, huh? You’ve got them at your school, too. That group with the cool-geek haircuts and the thrift shop clothes and names from fifties. Nice enough, never mean, but always the ones who end up being the Chosen One when the vampires come calling or when the alien queen needs the Source of All Light or something. They’re too cool to ever, ever do anything like go to prom or listen to music other than jazz while reading poetry. They’ve always got some story going on that they’re heroes of. The rest of us just have to live here, hovering around the edges, left out of it all, for the most part.” </i> <br><br>Actual rating: 3.25⭐️<br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Imagine your living in a town where weird things happen. Like one day the undead attacked, then there were soul eating ghosts and after this a really really weird vampire cycle of romance and death. <br>But your not like the indie kids, you aren’t in the middle of all the trouble. <br>No, your just a normal guy (well, at least he tries to be normal - and what does normal even mean?) who wants to go to prom with your friends and your best friend Hannah who you are in love with since a long time. <br>Even though it was kind of entertaining, it was also a bit boring. I didn’t really feel the story or the characters. I was just reading this book wanting to be finished with it and having no feeling at all about it. <br>Weird, I know. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456180221ra/18200627.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>There is Mikey our main character who’s in love with his best friend Hannah and haven’t told her anything about it. His mother wants to be a part of the US Congress and is pressuring her children into being perfect. <br>But Mikey and his sisters are nothing like perfect. No, they have anxieties and there have problems that sometimes could get them killed. <br>No, there are not perfect. <br>But they felt human. They had their problems and they had friends they could talk with. They had families and weird people at school. <br>Even though I liked the personalities of the characters, I didn’t love them. I liked them, that’s all. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️<br>Well, Mikey is in love with Hannah. And Hannah is in love with the new kid Nathan. <br>And Nathan is in love with... <br>Mel is flirting with people and Meredith, Mikey’s little sister, is crazy about a boy band. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515871165ra/24872568.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I fell in love with Patrick Ness writing when I read “A monster calls”. Even though I liked it in this book, it wasn’t as good as in “a monster calls”. <br>It was okay. Nice and readable. <br>I especially liked the parts with the paranormal stuff before a chapter started.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14274896039657999782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2825078463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2825078463" />
    <a title="sarah xoxo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57354360-sarah-xoxo"><img alt="sarah xoxo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567765387p2/57354360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2825078463?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sarah xoxo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sarah xoxo" href="/user/show/57354360-sarah-xoxo">sarah xoxo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2825078463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6243045242894709271"><b>The Rest of Us Just Live Here follows the kids on the sidelines. What everyone else is doing while the few 'chosen ones' are saving the world. The extras on TV shows. The normal people. </b><br/><br/>This book was basically a parody or satire of typical YA fantasy tropes. Chosen One main characters, love triangles, vampires, you name it. <br/><br/><i>“Because sometimes there are problems bigger than this week’s end of the world and sometimes you just have to find the extraordinary in your ordinary life.”</i> <br/><br/><b>We follow Mikey, </b></span>
  <span id="freeText6243045242894709271" style="display:none"><b>The Rest of Us Just Live Here follows the kids on the sidelines. What everyone else is doing while the few 'chosen ones' are saving the world. The extras on TV shows. The normal people. </b><br /><br />This book was basically a parody or satire of typical YA fantasy tropes. Chosen One main characters, love triangles, vampires, you name it. <br /><br /><i>“Because sometimes there are problems bigger than this week’s end of the world and sometimes you just have to find the extraordinary in your ordinary life.”</i> <br /><br /><b>We follow Mikey, a regular teenage boy just trying to get through his last year of high school. </b><br />When I say a regular teenage boy- I mean a regular teenage boy. He was boring and unexceptional. I suppose that was intended as we are following the everyday people after all, but it didn't make for a particularly impactful or engaging narrative.<br /><br /> I knew going in from the premise that there would likely be a lack of plot, but I was expecting the characters to add dimension and layers to the story. Unfortunately for me that didn't really happen. <br />The majority of the characters fell flat, and only had one or two defining personality traits with nothing else to flesh them out. <br /><br />Something I did love was the mental illness representation. Mikey has severe anxiety and OCD, and I think it is portrayed in a realistic way. I <i>loved </i>the scenes where he was talking to his therapist and enjoyed the way medication was treated. <br /><br /><i>“Feelings don't try to kill you, even the painful ones. Anxiety is a feeling grown too large. A feeling grown aggressive and dangerous. You're responsible for its consequences, you're responsible for treating it. But...you're not responsible for causing it. You're not morally at fault for it. No more than you would be for a tumor.” </i><br /><br />I found it quite unrealistic in terms of how the world was so similar to our own, and everyone just left the Indie Kids to do their thing. With social media and instant communications- I think they would likely have a much bigger impact on the political landscape, as well as general day to day lives of everyone. <br /><br />However, I read this as an audiobook compulsively, and flew through it. I was entertained most of the time while listening. It is just now, after finishing and having had time to mull over my thoughts that it feels quite forgettable. I initially rated this as 4 star after getting off the post-book high as I like to call it. I lowered my rating to 3 stars because that seems to better represent my feelings. <b>Above average, but not outstanding. </b><br /><br />Overall, if you are interested in the premise, I would still recommend it. Just be sure you know aren't expecting a fast paced plot or well explained fantasy elements. <br /><br /><i>“Not everyone has to be the Chosen One. Not everyone has to be the guy who saves the world. Most people just have to live their lives the best they can, doing things that are great for them, having great friends, trying to make their lives better, loving people properly. All the while knowing that the world makes no sense but trying to find a way to be happy anyway.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6243045242894709271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1135095697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135095697" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135095697?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135095697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17830007039565036204">A new Patrick Ness novel is always a big event and this was no less exciting. I avoided reading all reviews of the book before I started because I wanted to be surprised, especially as I know Patrick Ness has a habit of doing just that.<br/><br/>If you read a lot of young adult fantasy or science fiction, you'll have come across teenagers that fight vampires, wield magic and join rebel groups to fight against the government or zombies. They are known as the indie kids. <em>The Rest of Us Just Live Here</em> is abo</span>
  <span id="freeText17830007039565036204" style="display:none">A new Patrick Ness novel is always a big event and this was no less exciting. I avoided reading all reviews of the book before I started because I wanted to be surprised, especially as I know Patrick Ness has a habit of doing just that.<br /><br />If you read a lot of young adult fantasy or science fiction, you'll have come across teenagers that fight vampires, wield magic and join rebel groups to fight against the government or zombies. They are known as the indie kids. <em>The Rest of Us Just Live Here</em> is about the teenagers who live in the same world as the indie kids, but who are just trying to get through their everyday lives. Because they aren't the Chosen Ones.<br /><br /><em>The Rest of Us Just Live</em> here is a satire of young adult literature, but a friendly one. It's about the teenagers who aren't named Finn or Satchel, who aren't 'dying beautifully of cancer', and who aren't here to save the world. They're ordinary and their problems are ordinary and their friends and families are ordinary. But they're a joy to read about, especially as a fan of young adult contemporary fiction. I thoroughly enjoyed the concept and it made me feel a little odd, as if <em>I</em> were living in a world where all these fantastical things were happening in the background and I was just going about my life, talking about books on social media, going to the cinema and meeting friends for frozen yoghurt. At the beginning of each chapter, we're told all about the exciting and dangerous adventures the indie kids have been on, and they make an appearance in the normal lives of our protagonists because they're someone's friends and classmates, too.<br /><br /><em>The Rest of Us Just Live Here</em> is a well-written and wonderful exploration of what it's like to grow up. It's a mix of the closeness you feel to the characters in <em>Chaos Walking</em>, the sadness of <em>A Monster Calls</em>, and the delicate tackling of mental health in <em>More Than This</em>. I adore Mikey's little sister Meredith, who is much like me and my obsession with Taylor Swift. I enjoyed the friendship between Mikey and his best friend Jared, and watching him reveal his feelings for Henna. And I thought the way Patrick Ness approached anxiety and OCD – from showing the difference between obsession and compulsion, and the way anxiety can make someone feel like you're the one your friends could do without, to confirming that no one is to blame for their own mental health – was important and much-needed. <em>The Rest of Us Just Live Here</em> might not be as fast-paced as <em>Chaos Walking</em>, as mind-boggling as<em> More Than This</em> or as frightening as <em>A Monster Calls</em>, but it'll stay with you all the same.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to the publisher for providing this book for review!</i><br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17830007039565036204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
