<div id="review_1498873501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498873501" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498873501?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bad-beginning-loved-the-rest">bad-beginning-loved-the-rest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-but-not-quite-there-yet">great-but-not-quite-there-yet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=loved-while-reading-but-forgettable">loved-while-reading-but-forgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=love-wins">love-wins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498873501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13016982242642933155"><blockquote>
  <i>"They've always got some story going on that they're the heroes of. The rest of us just have to live here, hovering around the edges, left out of it all, for the most part."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I'm a little taken aback by <b>how much I enjoyed this little tale devoid of knives and murder and grand soundbites.</b> The Rest of Us Just Live Here, like its blurb advertises, is about normal kids doing normal stuff, encountering normal problems, while the Clarys and Meghans and Harrys fight supernatural stuff and have sweepi</span>
  <span id="freeText13016982242642933155" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"They've always got some story going on that they're the heroes of. The rest of us just have to live here, hovering around the edges, left out of it all, for the most part."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I'm a little taken aback by <b>how much I enjoyed this little tale devoid of knives and murder and grand soundbites.</b> The Rest of Us Just Live Here, like its blurb advertises, is about normal kids doing normal stuff, encountering normal problems, while the Clarys and Meghans and Harrys fight supernatural stuff and have sweeping adventures. <br><br>At the beginning of every chapter, we get a little peek into what the "indie kids"are up to. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Chapter the fourteenth, in which Satchel doubts the Prince's intentions towards her; he weeps, professing his eternal love, one that he's been waiting to give for millennia but had never found a repository for until he met Satchel."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479219740i/21161833.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Savage. Absolutely savage. Ness <b>pokes fun of YA tropes</b>, like how characters never seem to use the Internet (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462946110" rel="nofollow noopener">Hiya, Nora Grey</a>) and the weird names they have (Hiya, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16070143-teardrop" rel="nofollow noopener">Eureka</a>). <br><br>The protagonist Mike, on the other hand, struggles with his OCD. He helps his sister, who is a recovering anorexic. He takes his little sister to see a boy band. He has an alcoholic father and a mother who's running for Congress. Mundane stuff that Ness somehow makes interesting through <b>excellent characterization and by drawing on worries we have in our everyday lives.</b> What am I going to do after high school? What happens if me and my friends drift apart? We don't get definite endings for every plot line, but the book ends with a message of hope. Life goes on and you just roll with the punches, doing the best you can.<br><br>The diversity Ness weaves into the cast is awesome, too. But what I really want to praise is its <b>portrayal of mental illness.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Feelings don't try to kill you, even the painful ones. Anxiety is a feeling grown too large. A feeling grown aggressive and dangerous. You're responsible for its consequences, you're responsible for treating it. But Michael, you're not responsible for causing it. You're not morally at fault for it. No more than you would be for a tumor."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Taking medication isn't admitting defeat. It's usually healthy and necessary, and I wish more books showed it that way.<br><br>You can pretty much tell by how short this review is that I'm struggling to find the right words to pitch this book. I mean, it's <i>hard</i>. It's simply about ordinary kids living ordinary lives—but that doesn't make it any less extraordinary.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441920202ra/16168029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13016982242642933155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}" href="/user/show/64899539-sylvie-on-semi-hiatus">Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2401756761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17769808379318229493">The Rest of Us Just Live Here<br/>By Patrick Ness<br/><br/>3.25/5 Stars!<br/><br/>All I've heard of Patrick Ness were how wonderful and amazing his books are, so I decided to pick up one of his books and in this case it was 'The Rest of Us Just Live Here'.<br/><br/>This book was something I've never experienced with reading before, because instead of following the storyline of the heroes, it follows the normal people. The people who see everything happen and just have to continue their lives despite the demons, vampires and explo</span>
  <span id="freeText17769808379318229493" style="display:none">The Rest of Us Just Live Here<br />By Patrick Ness<br /><br />3.25/5 Stars!<br /><br />All I've heard of Patrick Ness were how wonderful and amazing his books are, so I decided to pick up one of his books and in this case it was 'The Rest of Us Just Live Here'.<br /><br />This book was something I've never experienced with reading before, because instead of following the storyline of the heroes, it follows the normal people. The people who see everything happen and just have to continue their lives despite the demons, vampires and exploding buildings. At the beginning of each chapter there is a brief overview of what happens to these 'heroes', the so-called 'indie kids', and then the story goes on. This group of friends aka the main characters: Mikey (has anexiety), his sister Mel (used to be anorexic), Henna (being controlled by her parents) and Jared (has some kind of godly powers) just want to graduate, and hope that the school will not explode again before they finish their senior year. Very original (credit to that) and fun, although I do not give it five stars, because the idea of the summary was better than the actual book.The whole plot was weirdly interesting, but it had so many clichés in it. <br /><br />What I didn't like about this book that the whole store ended with maybe's.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17769808379318229493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12464638095126533921">3.5 stars<br/><br/>This, by Patrick Ness standards, was a disappointment. After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786-more-than-this?from_search=true<br%20/>' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Than This</a> though, I really don't know how I expected any of his other books to measure up. <br/><br/>By regular standards this book really wasn't that bad. It was exactly what it advertised itself as. A book about the boring kids that are always stuck in the background and their boring lives. It was a boring book about the boring kids but it still managed to be relatable in a way that hurt the 16-year-old girl still living </span>
  <span id="freeText12464638095126533921" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />This, by Patrick Ness standards, was a disappointment. After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21969786-more-than-this?from_search=true&lt;br%20/&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than This</a> though, I really don't know how I expected any of his other books to measure up. <br /><br />By regular standards this book really wasn't that bad. It was exactly what it advertised itself as. A book about the boring kids that are always stuck in the background and their boring lives. It was a boring book about the boring kids but it still managed to be relatable in a way that hurt the 16-year-old girl still living inside of me. When I was 16, I was Mikey. It was almost painful to read about his struggles and for that extremely personal reason, I enjoyed this book. I wouldn't recommend it though. Go read More Than This, that book is a masterpiece. I'd suggest passing on this one though.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1604121641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1604121641" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1604121641?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1604121641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4676395940179213804">I'm not only surprised and delighted after reading this, but I was surprised and delighted *while* reading it from almost the very start.<br/><br/>I went, "Oh cool, it's almost like the UF YA version of a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13055592.Redshirts' title='Redshirts by John Scalzi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Redshirts</a> satire, where the Indie kids all die or don't while immortals create rifts in the high school universe and there's multiple Indie Flynns and gods and ghosts and vampires roam the halls, fall in love, and then die like little preeeecious flowers,... and everyone else just lives there. Satire! A </span>
  <span id="freeText4676395940179213804" style="display:none">I'm not only surprised and delighted after reading this, but I was surprised and delighted *while* reading it from almost the very start.<br /><br />I went, "Oh cool, it's almost like the UF YA version of a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13055592.Redshirts" title="Redshirts by John Scalzi" rel="nofollow noopener">Redshirts</a> satire, where the Indie kids all die or don't while immortals create rifts in the high school universe and there's multiple Indie Flynns and gods and ghosts and vampires roam the halls, fall in love, and then die like little preeeecious flowers,... and everyone else just lives there. Satire! A light, YA satire or even a full-on lampoon of the entire industry."<br /><br />I was hooked. I had only been reading a few pages.<br /><br />Little did I know that I could *then* begin reading it on multiple levels, even having our endearingly flawed non-Indie narrator spelling it out for us, that all the magic doesn't necessarily have to be real for us to believe it, but he does, and so does his friends, and that's cool and he doesn't have to believe our reality, either. :)<br /><br />*Jaw Drops*<br /><br />Okay! That's pretty damn well awesome and clearly stated and I can't love either interpretation more than I already do. <br /><br />And strangely enough, all these quirky-queer deer-god encounters only compliments and deepens the other half of the story, which is actually about finding your way to adulthood and exploring possibilities.<br /><br />But you ask, "Isn't that what all these UF YA novels do?"<br /><br />Sure, but I haven't read any that has been as self-consciously entertaining, creative, or straightforward about it. Ness knows the industry like a master. All those quirky flavors of the mass market teeny-books are expressed so deftly and interestingly in their own right, and I fairly stood up and started clapping at the chapter summaries... (Right before I began parsing how those chapter summaries *actually* fit into the real text. (Which is often not clear at first glance, but also completely unnecessary for our enjoyment of the text.:))<br /><br />I think Patrick Ness might be becoming one of those *always read* authors for me. I can't *not* trust that he'll be creative, clear, and a veritable master of his craft. Not only that, but I seem to be having a huge amount of fun every time I read his work. <br /><br />Okay, it's only up to two books, now, but you get the idea. Anyone who can hit a home run like this, twice out of two, has got my attention.<br /><br />Great stuff!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4676395940179213804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017508927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3747955144814930391">16/11/18: After a re-read I can for sure say I preferred this book the second time around so I’m increasing my rating from 3 to 4 stars. I feel I understood the stories more (there are two going on at once) and the ending was incredibly satisfying. I would recommend it if you want something a bit different.<br/>-<br/>-<br/>-<br/>-<br/>First Review 2016: I sadly didn’t like this one as much as some of Ness’ other books. I liked the plot but it didn’t stand out to me and just a couple weeks later I was already forgetting </span>
  <span id="freeText3747955144814930391" style="display:none">16/11/18: After a re-read I can for sure say I preferred this book the second time around so I’m increasing my rating from 3 to 4 stars. I feel I understood the stories more (there are two going on at once) and the ending was incredibly satisfying. I would recommend it if you want something a bit different.<br />-<br />-<br />-<br />-<br />First Review 2016: I sadly didn’t like this one as much as some of Ness’ other books. I liked the plot but it didn’t stand out to me and just a couple weeks later I was already forgetting important plot points from the story. Now about two? years after I can say I can’t remember a single thing about this story except a high school blows up? (It’s in the blurb, not really a spoiler) I have the audiobook so should be listening to it soon. I want to remember what this was about.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CBKcNuWKMK/mS7SLZTK5d2iCV343VRbjbLOdoxoggp7raFfrl3uIm6036yIE+R3YuHNMZCqwE/I8MN+8BDv1mA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('W62HM1pdTB+ybxliZytdRNBpG4brF6bDuC93EPVTSkC410zuKKz0K/kTRssG4PnrAJgAnPbyo9LorDUP60g9Rg==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4618940646444641652">Patrick Ness, an award-winning novelist, has written for England’s Radio 4 and <i>Sunday Telegraph</i> and is a literary critic for <i>The Guardian</i>. He has written many books, including the <i>Chaos Walking Trilogy</i>, <i>The Crash of Hennington</i>, <i>Topics About Which I Know Nothing</i>, and <i>A Monster Calls</i>. <br/> <br/>He has won numerous awards, including the Guardian Children’s Fiction Prize, the Booktrust Teenage Prize, and the C</span>
  <span id="freeText4618940646444641652" style="display:none">Patrick Ness, an award-winning novelist, has written for England’s Radio 4 and <i>Sunday Telegraph</i> and is a literary critic for <i>The Guardian</i>. He has written many books, including the <i>Chaos Walking Trilogy</i>, <i>The Crash of Hennington</i>, <i>Topics About Which I Know Nothing</i>, and <i>A Monster Calls</i>. <br /> <br />He has won numerous awards, including the Guardian Children’s Fiction Prize, the Booktrust Teenage Prize, and the Costa Children’s Book Award. Born in Virginia, he currently lives in London. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4618940646444641652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/42475450-the-rest-of-us-just-live-here">Quotes from The Rest of Us Ju...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Not everyone <i>has</i> to be the Chosen One. Not everyone has to be the guy who saves the world. Most people just have to live their lives the best they can, doing things that are great for <i>them</i>, having great friends, trying to make their lives better, loving people properly. All the while knowing that the world makes no sense but trying to find a way to be happy anyway.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7216702-not-everyone-has-to-be-the-chosen-one-not-everyone">334 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Feelings don't try to kill you, even the painful ones. Anxiety is a feeling grown too large. A feeling grown aggressive and dangerous. You're responsible for its consequences, you're responsible for <i>treating</i> it. But...you're not responsible for causing it. You're not morally at fault for it. No more than you would be for a tumor.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7242775-feelings-don-t-try-to-kill-you-even-the-painful-ones">311 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
